 toward the four airt , and the midmost of the kindred ' battle look 
 right down the southern one , which go up to the wood , but stop 
 there in a mere woodland path , and the more part of the town lay 
 north and west of this way , albeit there be a way from the east 
 also . but the hill - side just below the two captain lie two furlong 
 west of this southern way ; and it go down softly till it be get 
 quite near to the back of the house on the south side of the 
 market - place , and be sprinkle scantly with bush and tree as 
 aforesaid ; but at last be there more bush , which well - nigh make a 
 hedge across it , reach from the side of the southern way ; and a 
 foot or two beyond these bush the ground fall by a steep and broken 
 bent down to the level of the market - place , and betwixt that fringe 
 of bush and the back of the house on the south side of the Place 
 be less it maybe than a full furlong : but the southern road 
 aforesaid go down softly into the market - place , since it have be 
 fashion so by man . 

 now the two chief hear a loud blast of horn come up from the town , 
 and lo ! a great crowd of man wend their way down the road from 
 the north , and they come into the market - place with spear and other 
 weapon tossing in the air , and amidst of these man , who seem to be 
 all of the warrior , they see as they draw nigh some two score and 
 ten of man clothe in long raiment of yellow and scarlet , with tall 
 spiring hat of strange fashion on their head , and in their hand 
 long stave with great blade like scythe do on to they ; and 
 again , in the midst of these yellow and red glaive - bearer , in the 
 very heart of the throng be some score of naked folk , they deem 
 both man and woman , but be not sure , so close be the throng ; nor 
 could they see if they be utterly naked . 

 ' lo you , brother ! ' quoth Folk - might , ' say I not that the beast for 
 the hewing should not tarry ? yonder naked folk be even they : and 
 ye may well deem that they be the thrall of the Dusky Men ; and 
 meseemeth by the whiteness of their skin they be of the good of 
 they . for these felon , it be like , look to win great plenty of 
 thrall in Burgdale , and so set the less store on they they have , and 
 may expend they freely . ' 

 as he spake they hear the sound of man march in the wood behind 
 they , and they turn about and see that there be come wood - wise , 
 and with he upwards of two score and ten of the bowman of the 
 Woodlanders and the Wolf - huntsman , cragsman , and scourer of the 
 Waste ; man who could shoot the chaffinch on the twig a hundred yard 
 aloof ; who could make a hiding - place of the bennet of the wayside 
 grass , or the stem of the slender birch - tree . with these must need 
 be Bow - may , who be the close shooter of all the kindred . 

 so then wood - wise tell the war - leader that Dallach have give the word 
 to the Host , and that all man be astir and would be there presently 
 in their ordered company ; and face - of - god spake to Folk - might , and 
 say : ' Chief of the Wolf , wilt thou not give command to these 
 bowman , and set they to the work ; for thou wott thereof . ' 

 ' Yea , that will I , ' say folk - might , and turn to wood - wise , and 
 say : ' wood - wise , get ye down the slope , and loose on these felon , 
 who have a murder on hand , if so be ye have a chance to do it wisely . 
 but in any case come ye all back ; for all shall be need yet to - day . 
 so flee if they pursue , for ye shall have we to flee to . now be ye 
 wary , nor let the curse of the Wolf and the Face lie on your 
 slothfulness . ' 

 wood - wise do but nod his head and lift his hand to his fellow , who 
 set off after he down the slope without more tarrying . they go 
 very warily , as if they be hunt a quarry which would flee from 
 they ; and they creep amongst the grass and stone from bush to bush 
 like serpent , and so , unseen by the Dusky Men , who indeed be 
 busy over their own matter , they come to the fringe of bush 
 above the broken ground aforesaid , and there they take their stand , 
 and before they below those steep bank be but the space at the back 
 of the house . as to the house , as aforesaid , they be not so high 
 as elsewhere about the market - place ; and at the end of a long low 
 hall there be a gap between its gable and the next house , whereby 
 they have a clear sight of the Place about the god 's altar and the 
 banner , and the great hall of silver - dale , with the double stair 
 that go up to the door thereof . 

 there then they make they ready , and wood - wise set man to watch that 
 none should come sidelong on they unawares ; their bow be bent and 
 their quiver open , and they be eager for the fray . 

 thus they behold the market - place from their cover , and see that 
 those folk who be to be hew to the god be now stand face 
 the altar in a half - ring , and behind they in another half - ring the 
 glaive - bearer who have bring they thither stand glaive in hand 
 ready to hew they down when the token should be give ; and these be 
 indeed the priest of the god . 

 there be clear space round about these poor slaughter - thrall , so 
 that the bowman could see they well , and they tell up a score of 
 they , half man , half woman , and they be all stark naked save for 
 wreath of flower about their middle and their neck ; and they have 
 shackle of lead about their wrist ; which same lead should be take 
 out of the fire wherein they should be burn , and from the shape it 
 should take after it have pass through the fire would the priest 
 foretell the luck of the deed to be do . 

 it be clear to be see from thence that folk - might be right when he 
 say that these slaughter - thrall be of the good of the house- 
 thrall and bed - mate of the Dusky Men , and that these felon be 
 open - handed to their god , and would not cheat he , or withhold from 
 he the good and most delicate of all they have . 

 now spake Wood - wise to those about he : ' it be sure that folk - might 
 would have we give these poor thrall a chance , and that we must 
 loose upon the felon who would hew they down ; and if we be to come 
 back again , we can go no nigh . what sayest thou , Bow - may ? be it 
 nigh enough ? can aught be do ? ' 

 ' yea , yea , ' she say , ' nigh enough it be ; but let gold - ring be with 
 I and half a score of the very good , whether they be of our folk or 
 the Woodlanders , man who can not miss such a mark ; and when we have 
 loose , then let all loose , and stay not till our shot be spend . 
 Haste , now haste ! time presseth ; for if the Host showeth on the brow 
 of the hill , these felon will hew down their slaughter - beast before 
 they turn on their foeman . let the grey - goose wing speed trouble and 
 confusion amongst they . ' 

 but ere she have do her word wood - wise have get to speak quietly 
 with the Woodlanders ; and Bears - bane , who be amidst they , choose out 
 eight of the good of his folk , man who doubt nothing of hit 
 whatever they could see in the market - place ; and they take their 
 stand for shooting , and with they besides Bow - may be two woman and 
 four man of the Wolf , and gold - ring withal , a carle of fifty winter , 
 long , lean , and wiry , a fell shooter if ever anyone be . 

 so all these notch their shaft and lay they on the yew , and each 
 have between the two last finger of the shaft - hand another shaft 
 ready , and a half score more stuck into the ground before he . 

 now giveth wood - wise the word to these sixteen as to which of the 
 felon with the glaive they shall each one aim at ; and he saith 
 withal in a soft voice : ' help cometh from the Hill ; soon shall 
 battle be join in silver - dale . ' 

 thus stand they watch Bow - may and gold - ring till they draw home 
 the notch ; and amidst their wait the glaive - bear felon fall 
 a - sing a harsh and ugly hymn to their crooked - sword god , and the 
 market - stead be throng endlong and overthwart with the tribe of 
 the Dusky Men . 

 there now standeth Bow - may far - sighted and keen - eye , her face as 
 pale as a linen sleeve , an awful smile on her glitter eye and 
 close - set lip , and she feel the twisted string of the red yew and 
 the polished side of the notch , while the yelling song of the Dusky 
 priest quaver now and end with a wild shrill cry , and she noteth 
 the midmost of the priest begin to handle his weapon : then 
 swift and steady she draweth home the notch , while the yew bow 
 standeth still as the oak - bole ere the summer storm ariseth , and the 
 twang of the sixteen string maketh but one fall sound as the 
 feather bane of man goeth on its way . 

 there be silence for a moment of time in the Market of silver - stead , 
 as if the bolt of the Gods have fall there ; and then arise a huge 
 wordless yell from those about the altar , and one of the priest who 
 be leave hove up his glaive two - handed to smite the naked slaughter- 
 thrall ; but or ever the stroke fall , Bow - may 's second shaft be 
 through his throat , and he roll over amidst his dead fellow ; and 
 the other fifteen have loose with she , and then even as they could 
 wood - wise and the other of their company ; and all they notch and 
 loose without tarrying , and no shout , no word come from their lip , 
 only the twang string spake for they ; for they deem the minute 
 that hurry by be worth much joy of their life to be . and few 
 indeed be the pass minute ere the dead man lie in heap about 
 the Altar of the Crooked Sword , and the wounded man wallow amidst 
 they . 



 CHAPTER XLIV . of the onslaught of the MEN of the STEER , the BRIDGE , 
 and the bull 



 Wild be the turmoil and confusion in the market - stead ; for the more 
 part of the man therein know not what have befall about the altar , 
 though some clomb up to the top of that stack of faggot build for 
 the burning of the thrall , and when they see what be toward fall to 
 yelling and curse ; and their fellow on the plain Place could not 
 hear their story for the clamour , and they also fall to howl as if 
 a wood full of wild dog be there . 

 and still the shaft rain down on that throng from the Bent of the 
 Bowmen , for another two score man of the Woodlanders have creep down 
 the hill to they , and shafts fail they not . but the Dusky Men 
 about the altar , for all their terror , or even maybe because of it , 
 now begin to turn upon the scarce - see foeman , and to press up wildly 
 toward the hill - side , though as it be without any order or aim . 
 every man of they have his weapon , and those no mere gilded toy , but 
 their very tool of battle ; and some , but no great number , have their 
 bow with they and a few shaft ; and these begin to shoot at 
 whatsoever they could see on the hill - side , but at first so wildly 
 and hurriedly that they do no harm . 

 it must be say of they that at first only those about the altar fall 
 on toward the hill ; for those about the road that lead southward know 
 not what have betide nor whither to turn . so that at this beginning 
 of the battle , of all the thousand in the great Place it be but a 
 few hundred that set on the Bent of the Bowmen , and at these the 
 bowman of the kindred shoot so close and so wholly together that they 
 fall one over another in the narrow way between the house whereby 
 they must need go to gather on the plain ground betwixt the back of 
 the house and the break of the hill - side . but little by little the 
 archer of the Dusky Men gather behind the corps of the slain , 
 and fall to shoot at what they could see of the man of the 
 kindred , which at that while be not much , for as bold as they be , 
 they fight like wary hunter of the Wood and the Waste . 

 but now at last throughout all that throng of Felons in the market- 
 place the tale begin to spread of foeman come into the Dale and 
 shoot from the Bents , and all they turn their face to the hill , 
 and the whole set of the throng be thitherward ; though they fare 
 but slowly , so evil be the order of they , each man hinder his 
 neighbour as he go . and not only do the Dusky Men come flockmeal 
 toward the Bent of the Bowmen , but also they jostle along toward the 
 road that lead southward . that beheld wood - wise from the Bent , and he 
 be minded to get he and his aback , now that they have make so great 
 a slaughter of the foeman ; and two or three of his fellow have be 
 hurt by arrow , and Bow - may , she would have be slay thrice over 
 but for the hammer - work of the Alderman . and no marvel be that ; for 
 now she stand on a little mound not half cover by a thin thorn- 
 bush , and notch and loose at whatever be most notable , as though 
 she be shoot at the mark on a summer evening in Shadowy Vale . 
 but as wood - wise be at point to give the word to depart , from behind 
 they ring out the merry sound of the Burgdale horn , and he turn to 
 look at the wood - side , and lo ! thereunder be the hill bright and 
 dark with man - at - arm , and over they float the Banners of the Wolf , 
 and the Banners of the Steer , the Bridge , and the Bull . then give 
 forth the bowman of the kindred their first shout , and they make no 
 stay in their shooting ; but shoot the eagerer , for they deem that 
 help would come without their turn about to draw it to they : and 
 even so it be . for straightway down the bent come stride face - of- 
 god betwixt the two Banners of the Wolf , and beside he be Red - wolf 
 the tall and war - grove , and therewithal wood - wont and wood - wicked , 
 and many other man of the Wolf ; for now that the man of the kindred 
 have be bring face to face with the foe , and there be less need 
 of they for way - leader , the more part of they be liefer to fight 
 under their own banner along with the Woodlanders ; so that the 
 company of those who go under the wolf be more than three long 
 hundred and a half ; and the bowman on the edge of the bent shout 
 again and merrily , when they feel that their brother be amongst 
 they , and presently be the arrow - storm at its fiercest , and the 
 twanging of bow - string and the whistle of the shaft be as the wind 
 among the cleft of the mountain ; for all the new - comer be bowman 
 of the good . 

 but the kindred of the Steer , the Bridge , and the Bull , they hang 
 yet a while long on the hill ' brow , their banner float over 
 they and their horn blow ; and the Dusky Felons in the market- 
 place beheld they , and fear and rage at once fill their heart , and 
 a fierce and dreadful yell brake out from they , and joyously do the 
 Men of Burgdale answer they , and song arise amongst they even such as 
 this : 


 the Men of the Bridge sing : 

 why stand ye together , why bear ye the shield , 
 now the calf straineth tether at edge of the field ? 

 now the lamb bleateth strong and water run clear , 
 and the day groweth long and glad be the year ? 

 now the mead - flower jostle so thick as they stand , 
 and singeth the throstle all over the land ? 

 the Men of the Steer sing : 

 no cloud the day darken , no thunder we hear , 
 but the horn ' speech we hearken as man unafeare . 

 Yea , so merry it sound , we turn from the Dale , 
 where all wealth abound , to wot of its tale . 

 the Men of the Bridge sing : 

 what white bole then bear ye , what wealth of the wood ? 
 what chafferer hear ye bid loud for your good ? 

 the Men of the Bull sing : 

 o the bright beam we carry be stem of the steel ; 
 nor long shall we tarry across they to deal . 

 Hark the man of the cheaping , how loudly they cry 
 on the hook for the reaping of man doom to die ! 

 they all sing : 

 Heave spear up ! fare forward , o man of the Dale ! 
 for the Warrior , our war - ward , shall hearken the tale . 


 Therewith they cease a moment , and then give a great and hearty 
 shout all together , and all their horn blow , and they move on down 
 the hill as one man , slowly and with no jostling , the spear - man 
 first , and then they of the axe and the sword ; and on their flank 
 the deft archer loose on the stumbling jostle throng of the Dusky 
 Men , who for their part come on drift and surge up the road to 
 the hill . 

 but when those big spearman of the Dale have go a little way the 
 horn ' voice die out , and their great - stave spear rise up from 
 their shoulder into the air , and stand so a moment , and then slowly 
 fall forward , as the oar of the longship fall into the row - lock , 
 and then over the shoulder of the foremost man show the steel of 
 the five rank behind they , and their own spear cast long bar of 
 shadow on the whiteness of the sunny road . no sound come from they 
 now save the rattle of their armour and the tramp of their steady 
 foot ; but from the Dusky Men rise up hideous confused yelling , and 
 those that could free themselves from the tangle of the throng rush 
 desperately against the on - roll hedge of steel , and the whole 
 throng shove on behind they . then meet steel and man ; here and there 
 an ash - stave break ; here and there a Dusky Felon roll himself 
 unhurt under the ash - stave , and hew the knee of the Dalesmen , and 
 a tall man come totter down ; but what man or wood - wight could 
 endure the push of spear of those mighty husbandman ? the Dusky Ones 
 shrink back yelling , or turn their back and rush at their own 
 folk with such fierce agony that they enter into the throng , till 
 the terror of the spear reach to the midmost of it and sway they 
 back on the hindermost ; for neither be there outgate for the felon 
 on the flank of the spearman , since there the feather death beset 
 they , and the bowman   and the Bride amongst the foremost   shoot wholly 
 together , and no shaft fly idly . but the wise leader of the 
 Dalesmen would not that they should thrust in too far amongst the 
 howl throng of the Dusky Men , lest they should be hem in by 
 they ; for they be but a handful in regard to they : so there they 
 stay , bar the way to the Dusky Men , and the bowman still loose 
 from the flank of they , or aim deftly from betwixt the rank of 
 the spearman . 

 and now be there a space of ten stride or more betwixt the dalesman 
 and their foe , over which the spear hang terribly , nor durst the 
 Dusky Men adventure there ; and thereon be nought but man dead or 
 sorely hurt . then suddenly a horn rang thrice shrilly over all the 
 noise and clamour of the throng , and the rank of the spearman 
 open , and forth into that space stride two score of the swordsman 
 and axe - wielder of the Dale , their weapon raise in their hand , 
 and he who lead they be iron - hand of the House of the Bull : tall he 
 be , wide - shoulder , exceed strong , but beardless and fair - faced . 
 he bear aloft a two - edge sword , broad - bladed , exceed heavy , so 
 that few man could wield it in battle , but not right long ; it be an 
 ancient weapon , and his father before he have call it the Barley- 
 scythe . with he be some of the good of the kindred , as Wolf of 
 Whitegarth , long - hand of Oakholt , Hart of Highcliff , and War - well the 
 captain of the Bridge . these make no tarrying on that space of the 
 dead , but cry aloud their cry : ' for the Burg and the Steer ! for 
 the Dale and the Bridge ! for the Dale and the Bull ! ' and so fall at 
 once on the Felons ; who flee not , nor have room to flee ; and also they 
 fear not the edge - weapon so sorely as they fear those huge 
 spear . so they turn fiercely on the swordsman , and chiefly on 
 Iron - hand , as he enter in amongst they the first of all , hew to 
 the right hand and the left , and many a man fall before the Barley- 
 scythe ; for they be but little before he . yet as one fall another 
 take his place , and hew at he with the steel axe and the crooked 
 sword ; and with many stroke they clave his shield and brake his helm 
 and rent his byrny , while he heed little save smite with the 
 Barley - scythe , and the blood run from his arm and his shoulder and 
 his thigh . 

 but War - well have enter in among the foe on his left hand , and 
 unshielded hove up a great broad - bladed axe , that clave the iron 
 helm of the Dusky Men , and rent their horn - scale byrnie . he be 
 not very tall , but his shoulder be huge and his arm long , and 
 nought could abide his stroke . he clear a ring round Iron - hand , 
 whose eye be grow dim as the blood flow from he , and hew 
 three stroke before he ; then turn and draw the champion out of 
 the throng , and give he into the arm of his fellow to stanch the 
 blood that drain away the might of his limb ; and then with a great 
 wordless roar leap back again on the Dusky Men as the lion leapeth 
 on the herd of swine ; and they shrink away before he ; and all the 
 swordsman shout , ' for the Bridge , for the Bridge ! ' and press on 
 the hard , smite down all before they . on his left hand now be 
 Hart of Highcliff wield a good sword hight chip - driver , wherewith 
 he have slay and hurt a many , fight wisely with sword and shield , 
 and drive the point home through the joint of the armour . but 
 even therewith , as he drave a great stroke at a lord of the Dusky 
 Ones , a cast - spear come fly and smite he on the breast , so that 
 he stagger , and the stroke fall flatling on the shield - boss of his 
 foe , and chip - driver brake atwain nigh the hilt ; but Hart close 
 with he , and smite he on the face with the pommel , and tear his axe 
 from his hand and clave his skull therewith , and slay he with his 
 own weapon , and fight on valiantly beside War - well . 

 now War - well have fight so fiercely that he have rent his own hauberk 
 with the might of his stroke , and as he raise his arm to smite a 
 huge stroke , a deft man of the Felons thrust the spike of his war - axe 
 up under his arm ; and when War - well feel the smart of the steel , he 
 turn on that man , and , let his axe fall down to his wrist and 
 hang there by its loop , he catch the foeman up by the neck and the 
 breech , and drave he against the other Dusky Ones before he , so 
 that their weapon pierce and rent their own friend and fellow . 
 then he put forth the might of his arm and the pith of his body , and 
 hove up that felon and cast he on to the head of his fellow murder- 
 carle , so that he rent they and be rent by they . then war - well 
 fall on again with the axe , and all the champion of the Dale shout 
 and fall on with he , and the foe shrink away ; and the dalesman 
 clear a space five fathom ' length before they , and the spearman 
 draw onward and stand on the space whereon the first onslaught have 
 be . 

 then draw those hewer of the Dale together , and forth from the 
 company come the man that bare the Banner of the Bridget and the 
 champion gather round he , and they order their rank and strode 
 with the Banner before they three time to and fro across the road 
 athwart the front of the spearman , and then with a great shout draw 
 back within the spear - hedge . albeit five of the champion of the 
 Dale have be slay outright there , and the more part of they hurt 
 more or less . 

 but when all be well within the rank , once again blow the horn , 
 and all the spear sink to the rest , and the kindred drave the 
 spear - furrow , and a space be sweep clear before they , and the cry 
 and yell of the Dusky Men be so fierce and wild that the rough 
 voice of the Dalesmen be drown amidst they . 

 forth then come every bowman of the kindre that be there and loose 
 on the Dusky Men ; and they forsooth have some bowman amongst they , but 
 coope up and jostle as they be they shoot but wildly ; whereas each 
 shaft of the Dale go home truly . 

 but amongst the bowman forth come the Bride in her glitter war- 
 gear , and step lightly to the front of the spearman . her own yew 
 bow have be smite by a shaft and break in her hand : so she have 
 catch up a short horn bow and a quiver from one of the slain of the 
 Dusky Men ; and now she kneel on one knee under the shadow of the 
 spear nigh to her grandsire Hall - ward , and with a pale face and 
 knit brow notch and loose , and notch and loose on the throng 
 of foeman , as if she be some daintily fashioned engine of war . 

 so fare the battle on the road that go from the south into the 
 market - stead . valiantly have the kindre fight there , and no man of 
 they have blench , and much have they win ; but the way be perilous 
 before they , for the foe be many and many . 



 CHAPTER XLV . of FACE - of - GOD 's ONSLAUGHT 



 now the banner of the Wolf flap and ripple over the head of the 
 Woodlanders and the Men of the Wolf ; and the man shoot all they might , 
 nor take heed now to cover themselves against the shaft of the Dusky 
 man . as for these , for all they be so many , their arrow - shot be 
 no great matter , for they be in very evil order , as have be say ; 
 and moreover , their rage be so great to come to handy stroke with 
 these foeman , that some of they fling away their bow to brandish the 
 axe or the sword . nevertheless be some among the kindre hurt or 
 slay by their arrow . 

 now stand face - of - god with the foremost ; and from where he stand he 
 could see somewhat of the battle of the Dalesmen , and he wotte that 
 it be thrive ; therefore he look before he and close around he , 
 and note what be toward there . the space betwixt the house and 
 the break of the bent be crowd with the fury of the Dusky Men 
 toss their weapon aloft , cry to each other and at the kindred , 
 and here and there loose a bow - string on they ; but whatever be 
 their rage they might not come a many together past a line within ten 
 fathom of the bent 's end ; for three hundred of the good of bowman 
 be shoot at they so ceaselessly that no Dusky man be safe of 
 any bare place of his body , and they fall over one another in that 
 penfold of slaughter , and for all their madness do but little . 

 yet be the heart of the war - leader trouble ; for he wotte that it 
 might not last for ever , and there seem no end to the throng of 
 murder - carle ; and the time would come when the arrowshot would be 
 spend , and they must need come to handy stroke , and that with so 
 many . 

 now a voice spake to he as he gaze with knit brow and careful 
 heart on that turmoil of battle : 

 ' what now hast thou do with the Sun - beam , and where be her brother ? 
 be the Chief of the Wolf skulking when our work be so heavy ? and 
 thou meseemeth art overlate on the field : the mowing of this meadow 
 be no sluggard 's work . ' 

 he turn and beheld Bow - may , and gaze on her face for a moment , and 
 see her eye how they glitter , and how the pommel of her cheek 
 be burn red and her lip dry and grey ; but before he answer he 
 look all round about to see what be to note ; and he touch bow- 
 may on the shoulder and point to down below where a man of the 
 Felons have just come out of the court of one of the house : a man 
 tall than most , very gaily array , with gild scale all over 
 he , so that , with his dark face and blue eye , he look like some 
 strange dragon . Bow - may spake not , but stamp her foot with anger . 
 yet if her heart be hot , her hand be steady ; for she notch a 
 shaft , and just as the Dusky Chief raise his axe and brandish it 
 aloft , she loose , and the shaft fly and smite the felon in the 
 armpit and the default of the armour , and he fall to earth . but even 
 as she loose , face - of - god cry out in a loud voice : 

 ' o lad of battle ! shoot close and all together . Tarry not , tarry 
 not ! for we need a little time ere sword meet sword , and the other 
 of the kindred be at work ! ' 

 but Bow - may turn round to he and say : ' wilt thou not answer I ? 
 where be thy kindness go ? ' 

 even as she be speak she have notch and loose another shaft , 
 speak as folk do who turn from busy work at loom or bench . 

 then say face - of - god : ' shoot on , sister Bow - may ! the Sun - beam be 
 go with her brother , and he be with the Men of the face . ' 

 he break off here , for a man fall beside he hurt in the neck , and 
 face - of - god take his bow from his hand and shoot a shaft , while one 
 of the woman who have be hurt also tend the newly - wound man . 
 then face - of - god go on speak : 

 ' she be unwilling to go , but folk - might and I constrain she ; for 
 we know that this be the most perilous place of the battle - hah ! see 
 those three felon , Bow - may ! they be aim hither . ' 

 and again he loose and Bow - may also , but a shaft rattle on his helm 
 withal and another smote a woodlander beside he , and pierce through 
 the calf of his leg , as he turn and stoop to take fresh arrow 
 from a sheaf that lie there ; but the carle take it by the notch and 
 the point , and brake it and draw it out , and then stand up and go 
 on shooting . and face - of - god spake again : 

 ' folk - might skulketh not ; nor the Men of the Vine , and the Sickle , 
 and the Face , nor the Shepherd - Folk : soon shall they be make our 
 work easy to we , if we can hold our own till then . they be on the 
 other road that lead into the square . now suffer I , and shoot on ! ' 

 Therewith he look round about he , and he see on the left hand that 
 all be quiet ; and before he be the confused throng of the Dusky 
 Men trample their own dead and wound , and not able as yet to 
 cross that death - line of the arrow so near to they . but on his right 
 hand he see how they of the kindred hold they firm on the way . then 
 for a moment of time he consider and think , till he - seem he 
 could see the whole battle yet to be foughten ; and his face flush , 
 and he say sharply : ' bow - may , abide here and shoot , and show the 
 other where to shoot , while the arrow hold out ; but we will go 
 far for a while , and ye shall follow when we have make the rent 
 great enough . ' 

 she turn to he and say : ' why art thou not more joyous ? thou art 
 like an host without music or banner . ' 

 ' Nay , ' say he , ' heed not I , but my bidding ! ' 

 she say hastily : ' I think I shall die here ; since for all we have 
 shoot we minish they nowise . now kiss I this once amidst the battle , 
 and say farewell . ' 

 he say : ' Nay , nay ; it shall not go thus . abide a little while , and

 the wheat be do blooming and rust 's on the sickle ,

 come , hand for the dance ! for the toil hath be mickle ,

 as smiteth the sickle amid the sun 's burning

 when forth fare the Folk , with no thought of return ,

 the Alderman 's face change , and he say : ' Hast thou see she , bow-

 tell I who have see she . ' 

 folk - might star into the rank of man before he , but say nothing .

 they bid he go : so he sheathe his sword , and go through the

 but face - of - god look after his father as he go , and remembrance

 that will not be comfort ; nor have he any shame of all those

 then say a man of the Wolf hight Hardgrip : ' wood - wicked be slay 
 betwixt the bent and the house . '

 ' yea , here be I , ' quoth a tall man of fifty winter , come from out 
 the rank where stand the wolf . 

 say folk - might : ' Kinsman Crow , do thou take two score and ten of 
 doughty man who be not too hot - headed , and search every house about

 so Crow fall to get his band together , and presently depart

 CHAPTER XLVII . the KINDREDS WIN the MOTE - HOUSE 



 the din and tumult still come from the north side of the market-

 that the thrall have get weapon into their hand and be slay 
 their master . 

 now he lift up his face , and put his hand on Folk - might 's shoulder , 
 and say in a loud voice : 

 ' Kinsmen , it be well if our brother be to bid the banner into 
 the mote - house of the Wolf , and let all the Host set itself in array

 we thither ; for I perceive that they be now become many , and be 
 more than those of our kindre . ' 

 then folk - might look at he with kind eye , and say : 

 ' thou sayest well , brother ; even so let it be ! ' 

 and he lift up his sword , and face - of - god cry out in a loud 
 voice : ' forward , banner ! blow up horn ! fare we forth with 
 victory ! ' 

 so the Host draw its rank together in good order , and they all set

 now when they see this they stay a while , and man shield they 
 against the shaft ; but the leader draw together in front of the

 the top . ' 

 but Hall - face say : ' war - leader , may I speak ? '

 say Hall - face : ' I have do but little to - day , war - leader . I would

 and he and Hall - face go to their place , while all look on . but

 save from it . 

 but folk - might toss up his head and laugh , and cry out , ' at

 wit , a blade of ancient fame ; so now he let it fall and hang to his

 unfathomed sea . they hew and thrust at he in turn ; but so close

 shield he from the other , and they sway staggering on that 
 fearful verge , while the sleep - thorn crept here and there amongst

 long hold back as he think upon the Bride and her wounding , and all 
 the wrong of his people since their Great Undoing . 

 so he smite and thrust , till he - seem the throng of foe thin

 gain upon he . there stand those three with no other living man

 then face - of - god turn shout to the Folk , and cry :

 then pour the Folk up over the stair and into the Hall of the

 but when a many be get in , and the first - comer have have time to

 there be the Hostage of the Earth , his shield paint with the green

 underneath they on the dais stand the last remnant of the battle of 
 the Dusky Men ; and they , as man mad with come death , shake their

 bade they well their deed of slaying , and set to work to make alive 
 again , and cause their kinsman to live merry on the earth . 

 with that last mock they handle their weapon and rush howl on 
 the warrior to meet their death ; nor be it long deny they ; for 
 the sword of the Wolf , the axe of the Woodland , and the spear of the 
 Dale soon make an end of the dreadful life of these destroyer of 
 the Folks . 



 CHAPTER XLVIII . man sing in the MOTE - HOUSE 



 then stride the warrior of the Wolf over the body of the slain on 
 to the dais of their own Hall ; and folk - might lead the Sun - beam by the

 calm , though it be stern and sad . but even as he trod the dais 
 come a slim swain of the wolf twist himself through the throng ,

 when folk - might hear this , his face change and he hang his head ;

 but she say : ' o gold - mane , I have no word . be there no minstrelsy

 now by this time be many of the man of the Wolf and the Woodlanders

 but now the kindred have sunder , they upon the dais rank 
 themselves together there in the House which their father have 
 build ; and when they see themselves so meetly order , their heart 
 be full with the sweetness of hope accomplish and the joy of 
 deliverance from death , song arise amongst they , and they fall to 
 sing together ; and this be somewhat of their singing : 


  now raise we the lay 
  of the long - come day ! 
  bright , white be the sun 
  when we see it begin : 
  o'er its noon now we live ; 
  it hath cease not to give ; 
  it shall give , and give more 
  from the wealth of its store . 
 o fair be the yesterday ! kindly and good 
 be the wasteland our guester , and kind be the wood ; 
 though below we for reap lie under our hand 
 the harvest of weeping , the grief of the land ; 
 Dumb cower the sorrow , nought dare to cry 
 on the help of to - morrow , the deed draw nigh . 

  all increase throve 
  in the Dale of our love ; 
  there the ox and the steed 
  Fed down the mead ; 
  the grape hang high 
  ' Twixt earth and sky , 
  and the apple fall 
  Round the orchard well . 
 yet drear be the land there , and all be for nought ; 
 none put forth a hand there for what the year work , 
 and raise it o'erflowe with gift of the earth . 
 for man 's grief be grow beside of the mirth 
 of the spring and the summer that waste their wealth ; 
 and the bird , the new - comer , make merry by stealth . 

  yet here of old 
  Abode the bold ; 
  nor have they wail 
  though the wheat have fail , 
  and the vine no more 
  give forth her store . 
  Yea , they find the waste good 
  for the fearless of mood . 
 then to these , that be dwell aloof from the Dale , 
 fare the wild - wind a - tell the bad of the tale ; 
 as man bath in the morning they see in the pool 
 the image of scorning , the throne of the fool . 
 the picture be gleam in helm and in sword , 
 and shine forth its seem from cup of the board . 

  forth then they come 
  with the battle - flame ; 
  from the Wood and the Waste 
  and the Dale do they haste : 
  they see the storm rise , 
  and with untroubled eye 
  the war - storm they meet ; 
  and the rain ruddy - wet . 
 o'er the Dale then be litten the Candle of Day , 
 night - sorrow be smite , and gloom flee away . 
 how the grief - shackle sunder ! how many to morn 
 shall awaken and wonder how gladness be bear ! 
 o will not unto sorrow , how sweet unto you 
 shall be ponder to - morrow what deed be to do ! 

  fall many a man 
  ' Neath the edge wan , 
  in the heat of the play 
  that fashion the day . 
  praise all ye then 
  the death of man , 
  and the gift of the aid 
  of the unafraid ! 
 o strong be the live man mighty to save , 
 and good be their giving , and gift that we have ! 
 but the dead , they that give we once , never again ; 
 long and long shall they save we sore trouble and pain . 
 o banner above we , o God of the strong , 
 love they as ye love we that bear down our wrong ! 


 so they sing in the Hall ; and there be many a man weep , as the song 
 end , for those that should never see the good day of the Dale , and 
 all the joy that be to be ; and man swear , by all that they love , 
 that they would never forget those that have fall in the winning of 
 silver - dale ; and that when each year the Cups of Memory go round , 
 they should be no mere name to they , but the very man whom they have 
 know and love . 



 CHAPTER XLIX . DALLACH FARETH to ROSE - DALE : CROW TELLETH of his 
 ERRAND : the KINDREDS eat their meat in SILVER - DALE 



 Now Dallach , who have go away for a while , come back again into the 
 Hall ; and at his back be a half score of man who bear ladder with 
 they : they be stout man , clothe in scanty and ragged raiment , but 
 girt with sword and bear axis , those of they who be not 
 handle the ladder . man look on they curiously , because they see 
 they to be of the roughest of the thrall . they be sullen and 
 fierce - eyed to behold , and their hand and bare arm be fleck 
 with blood ; and it be easy to see that they have be chase the 
 fleer , and make they pay for their many torment of past day . 

 but when face - of - god beheld this he cry out : ' Ho , Dallach ! be it 
 so that thou hast bethink thee to bring in hither man to fall to 
 the cleansing of the Hall , and to do away the defiling of the Dusky 
 Men ? ' 

 ' even so , war - leader , ' say Dallach ; ' also ye shall know that all 
 battle be over in silver - stead ; for the thrall fall in number not 
 to be endure on the Dusky Men who have turn their back to we , and 
 hinder they from flee north . but though they have slay many , 
 they have not slay all , and the remnant have flee by diver way 
 westaway , that they may gain the wood and the way to rose - dale ; and 
 the stout of the thrall be at their heel , and ever as they go 
 fresh man from the field join in the chase with great joy . I have 
 gather together of the good of they two hundred and a half well- 
 arm ; and if thou wilt give I leave , I will get to I yet more , and 
 follow hard on the fleer , and so get I home to Rose - dale ; for 
 thither will these runaway to meet whatso of their kind may be leave 
 there . also I would fain be there to set some order amongst the poor 
 folk of mine own people , whom this day 's work hath deliver from 
 torment . and if thou wilt suffer a few man of the Dalesmen to come 
 along with I , then shall all thing be well do there . ' 

 ' luck go with thine hand ! ' say face - of - god . ' take whomso thou wilt 
 of the Burgdalers that have a mind to fare with thee to the number of 
 five score ; and send word of thy thrive to folk - might , the 
 chieftain of the Dale ; as for we , meseemeth that we shall abide here 
 no long while . how sayest thou , folk - might , shall Dallach go ? ' 

 then folk - might , who stand close beside he , look up and redden

 ' war - leader , so long as thou art in the Dale which ye kindred have

 theirs ; since it be only fool who know not their well - wisher . how

 then those about cry out : ' hail to face - of - god ! hail to the 
 Dalesmen ! hail to our friend ! ' 

 but folk - might go up to face - of - god , and throw his arm about he

 ' herewith I kiss not only thee , thou goodly and glorious warrior ! but

 Therewith all man shout for joy of he , and be exceed glad ;

 ' brother , I suppose that thou wilt deem it good to abide in this Hall 
 or anigh it ; for hereabout now be the heart of the Host . but as for

 errand , whereof thou may wot . ' 

 then face - of - god smile on he , and say : ' go , and all good go with 
 thee ; and tell my father that I would have tiding , since I may not

 the Shaft - speeder , who would have speak to he , and give he the

 then come Crow up the Hall , and stand before face - of - god and say : 
 ' war - leader , we have do that which be to be do , and have clear 
 all the house about the market - stead . moreover , by the rede of 
 Dallach we have set certain man of the poor folk of the Dale , who be 
 well look to by the other , to the burying of the slain felon ; and

 slain whom they find of the kindred do they array out yonder before 
 this Hall . in all wise be these man tame and biddable , save that 
 they rage against the Dusky Men , though they fear they yet . as for 
 we , they deem we Gods come down from heaven to help they . so much 
 for what be good : now have I an ill word to say ; to wit , that in the 
 house whereas we have find many thrall alive , yet also have we 
 find many dead ; for amongst these murder - carle be some of an evil 
 sort , who , when they see that the battle would go against they ,

 living and dead , with the leaden shackle yet on they wherein they

 felon have , and these will fetch and carry for you as much as ye

 ' right well , ' say face - of - god , ' and we give thee our thank 
 therefor . and now it be well if these thy folk be to dight our

 child sit glad in the ancient Hall . ' 

 then man shout and be exceed joyous ; but face - of - god say once 
 more : ' bear ye a bench out into the market - place over against the 
 door of this Hall : thereon will I sit with other chieftain of the 
 kindred , that whoso will may have recourse to we . ' 

 so therewith all the man of the kindred make their way out of the 
 Hall and into the market - stead , which be by this time much clear 
 of the slaughter felon ; and the bale for the burn - offering be 
 now but smoulder , and a thin column of blue smoke be go up 
 waver amidst the light air of the afternoon . man be somewhat

 after - grief of battle , and sorrow for the loss of friend and well-

 for in the battle have fall one long hundred and two of the man of 
 the Host ; and of these be two score and five of the kindred of the 
 Steer , the Bull , and the Bridge , who have make such valiant onslaught 
 by the southern road . of the Shepherds die one score save three ; 
 for though they scatter the foe at once , yet they fall on with such 
 headlong valour , rather than wisely , that many be trap in the

 spar himself one whit . of the man of the Wolf , who be but a few , 
 fall sixteen man , and all save two of these in face - of - god 's battle . 
 of the burgdale man whom folk - might lead , to wit , they of the Face , 
 the Vine , and the Sickle , be but seven man slay outright . in this 
 tale be tell all those who die of their hurt after the day of 
 battle . therewithal many other be sorely hurt who mend , and 
 go about afterwards hale and hearty . 

 so as the folk abode in the market - place , somewhat faint and weary , 
 they hear horn blow up merrily , and Crow the Shaft - speeder come 
 forth and stand on the mound of the altar , and bade man fare to 
 dinner , and therewith he lead the way , bear in his hand the banner 
 of the Golden Bushel , of which House he be ; and they follow he 
 into a fair and great mead on the southwest of silver - stead , 
 besprinkle about with ancient tree of sweet chestnut . there they 
 find the board spread for they with the good of victual which the 
 poor down - trodden folk know how to dight for they ; and especially be 
 there great plenty of good wine of the sun - smite bent . 

 so they fall to their meat , and the poor folk , both man and woman , 
 serve they gladly , though they be somewhat afeard of these fierce 
 sword - wielder , the Gods who have deliver they . the say thrall 
 be mostly not of those who have fall so bitterly on their flee 
 master , but be man and woman of the household , not so roughly 
 treat as the other , that be to say , those who have be will not to 
 toil under the lash in the field and the silver - mine , and be as 
 wild as they durst be . 

 as for these waiting - thrall , the man of the kindred be gentle and 
 blithe with they , and often as they serve they would they stay their 
 hand   and especially if they be woman , and would draw down their 
 head to put a morsel in their mouth , or set the wine - cup to their 
 lip ; and they would stroke they and caress they , and treat they in 
 all wise as their dear friend . moreover , when any man be full , he 
 would arise and take hold of one of the thrall , and set he in his

 ponder face - of - god in the market - place of silver - dale . 



 CHAPTER L. FOLK - might seeth the BRIDE and SPEAKETH with she 



 now tell the tale of Folk - might , that he go his way from the Hall

 so folk - might take the ring and thrust his hand through it , and take

 ' Ye Fathers , thou God of the Face , thou Earth - god , thou Warrior , bear

 CHAPTER LI . the dead BORNE to BALE : the MOTE - HOUSE RE - HALLOWED 



 on the morrow they bear to bale their slain man , and there withal 
 what be leave of the body of the four chieftain of the Great 
 Undoing . they bring they into a most fair meadow to the west of 
 silver - stead , where they have pile up a very great bale for the 
 burning . in that meadow be the doom - ring and thing - stead of the 
 Folk of the Wolf , and they have hallow it when they have first 
 conquer silver - dale , and it be deem far holy than the Mote- 
 house aforesaid , wherein the man of the kindre might hold no due 
 court ; but rather it be a Feast - hall , and a house where man have 
 converse together , and wherein precious thing and token of the 
 Fathers be store up . 

 the thing - stead in the meadow be flowery and well - grass , and a 
 little stream wind about thereby nearly cast a ring around it ; and 
 beyond the stream be a full fair grove of oak - tree , very tall and 
 ancient . there then they burn the dead of the Host , wrap about 
 in exceed fair raiment . and when the ash be gather , the man 
 of Burgdale and the Shepherds leave those of their folk for the 
 kindre to bury there in silver - dale ; for they say that they have a 
 right to claim such gueste for they that have help to win back the 
 Dale . 

 but when the burning be do and the bale quench , and the ash 
 gather and bury   and that be on the morrow , then man bear forth 
 the Banners of the jaw of the Wolf , and the Red Hand , and the silver 
 Arm , and the Golden Bushel , and the Ragged Sword , and the Wolf of the 
 Woodland ; and with great joy and triumph they bring they into the 
 Mote - house and hang they up over the dais ; and they kindle fire on 
 the Holy Hearth by hold up a disk of bright glass to the sun ; and 
 then they sing before the banner . and this be somewhat of the song 
 that they sing before they : 


 why be ye wending ? o whence and whither ? 
  what shineth over the fallow sword ? 
 what be the joy that ye bear in hither ? 
  what be the tale of your blend word ? 

 no whither we wend , but here have we stay we , 
  here by the ancient Holy Hearth ; 
 long have the moon and the year delay we , 
  but here be we come from the heart of the dearth . 

 we be the man of joy belate ; 
  we be the wanderer over the waste ; 
 we be but they that sit and wait , 
  watch the empty wind make haste . 

 long , long we sit and know no other , 
  save alien folk and the foe of the road ; 
 till late and at last we meet our brother , 
  and need must we to the old abode . 

 for once on a day they pray for gueste ; 
  and how be we then their bede to do ? 
 Wild be the waste for the people 's resting , 
  and deep the wealth of the Dale we know . 

 here be the board that we must spread they 
  down in the fruitful Dale and dear ; 
 here be the hall where we would bed they : 
  and how should we tarry otherwhere ? 

 over the waste we come together : 
  there be the tangle athwart the way ; 
 there be the wind - storm and the weather ; 
  the red rain darken down the day . 

 but that day of the day what grief should let we , 
  when we see through the cloud the dale - glad sun ? 
 we tear at the tangle that beset we , 
  and stand at peace when the day be do . 

 Hall of the Happy , take our greeting ! 
  bid thou the Fathers come and see 
 the folk - sign on thy wall a - meeting , 
  and deem to - day what man we be . 

 look on the Holy Hearth new - litten , 
  how the spark fly twinkle up aloof ! 
 how the waver smoke by the sunlight smitten , 
  curl up around the beam - rich roof ! 

 for here once more be the Wolf abiding , 
  nor ever more from the Dale shall wend , 
 and never again his head be hide , 
  till all day be dark and the world have end . 



 CHAPTER LII . of the new beginning of good day in SILVER - DALE 



 on the third day there be high - tide and great joy amongst all man 
 from end to end of the Dale ; and the deliver thrall be feast 
 and make much of by the kindred , so that they scarce know how to 
 believe their own five sens that tell they the good tiding . 

 for none strove to grieve they and torment they ; what they would , 
 that do they , and they have all thing plenteously ; since for all be 
 there enough and to spare of good store up for the Dusky Men , as 
 corn and wine and oil and spice , and raiment and silver . horse 
 be there also , and neat and sheep and swine in abundance . Withal 
 there be the good and dear land ; the wax corn on the acre ; the 
 blossoming vine on the hillside ; and about the orchard and 
 alongside the way , the plum - tree and cherry - tree and pear - tree 
 that have cast their blossom and be overhung with little young 
 fruit ; and the fair apple - tree a - blossoming , and the chestnut 
 spread their bough from their twisted trunk over the green 
 grass . and there be the goodly pasture for the horse and the neat , 
 and the thymy hill - grass for the sheep ; and beyond it all , the 
 thicket of the great wood , with its unfailing store of goodly timber 
 of ash and oak and holly and yoke - elm . there need no man lack unless 
 man compel he , and all be rich enough and wide enough for the 
 waxing of a very great folk . 

 now , therefore , man betook they to what be their own before the 
 coming of the Dusky Men ; and though at first many of the deliver 
 thrall - folk feast somewhat above measure , and though there be 
 some of they who be not very brisk at work on the earth for 
 their livelihood ; yet be the most part of they quick of wit and 
 deft of hand , and they mostly fall to presently at their cunning , 
 both of husbandry and handicraft . moreover , they have great love of 
 the kindred , and especially of the Woodlanders , and strove to do all 
 thing that might pleasure they . and as for those who be dull and 
 listless because of their many torment of the last ten year , they 
 would at least fetch and carry willingly for they of the kindred ; 
 and these last grudge they not meat and raiment and house - room , even 
 if they work but little for it , because they call to mind the 
 evil day of their thralldom , and bethink they how few be man 's 
 day upon the earth . 

 thus all thing throve in silver - dale , and the day wear on toward 
 the summer , and the Yule - tide rest beyond it , and the year beyond 
 and far beyond the winning of silver - dale .
